SE Bengaluru
HD Danske Bank sets up IT unit in Bengaluru
WC 185 words
PD 3 July 2015
SN The Times of India
SC TOI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 The Times of India Group

LP 

BENGALURU: Danske Bank, a leading financial enterprise in Europe and one of the largest banks in Denmark, has established an IT and support services centre in Bengaluru.

The centre, in collaborated with ITC Infotech, is the bank’s first service centre in Asia and will provide development and support for its banking services.

TD 

Speaking at a press conference on Wednesday, Jim Ditmore, COO of services and IT group, said, “We are very pleased to work with ITC. There is a need of critical delivery of mobile services and we look to leverage it with this.” He also said the bank may look to set up a banking representative office in India in the future, to help serve customers better.

The bank has hired around 800 people for the Bengaluru centre. The centre can accommodate 1,200 people and more hiring will happen as demand for IT services increases. The company has mostly hired those with MCA and engineering degrees. The Bengaluru centre will aim to provide digital services and better software.

For Reprint Rights: timescontent.com

HD Danske Bank Oyj Statement Re Danske Bank Is A Systemically Important Financial Institution In Finland
WC 380 words
PD 6 July 2015
ET 05:30
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
TIDM89KN 
 
   Danske Bank Plc 
 
   Company announcement 
 
   6 July 2015 
 
   Danske Bank is a systemically important financial institution in Finland 
 
   According to a decision published today, the Financial Supervisory 
Authority has designated Danske Bank Plc as a systemically important 
financial institution (other systemically important institution, O-SII) 
for the Finnish national financial system as referred to in the Act on 
Credit Institutions. In conjunction with this, the Financial Supervisory 
Authority imposed a 0,5%'s capital add-on, which will enter into force 
on 7 January 2016, on Danske Bank Plc on account of its systemic 
importance. 
 
   European financial supervisors annually assess and rate the institutions 
operating within their jurisdiction. The European Central Bank (ECB) had 
already previously designated Danske Bank Plc as a systemically 
important bank, and Danske Bank Plc's supervision was transferred to the 
ECB in November 2014. 
 
   "The Financial Supervisory Authority's designation confirms that Danske 
Bank plays a major role in the Finnish banking system and as a trusted 
banking partner for Finnish customers. Danske Bank Plc's capital 
adequacy is strong, and the capital add-on does not affect our ability 
to serve Finnish bank customers. Danske Bank's aim is to grow in Finland, 
and our strong capital adequacy provides a good foundation for this," 
says Risto Tornivaara, CEO of Danske Bank Plc. 
 
 
 
   Further information: 
 
   Risto Tornivaara, CEO, Danske Bank Plc 
 
   For an interview with Risto Tornivaara, please contact Irja Kukkola tel. 
+358 10 546 8006. 
 
   Distribution: 
 
   NASDAQ OMX Helsinki 
 
   London Stock ExchangeLuxembourg Stock Exchange 
 
   Major media

   This is a translation of a company announcement in the Finnish language. 
In case of discrepancies, the Finnish version prevails.

SE Business
HD Maersk Sells Stake in Offshore Oil Services Company Esvagt; Maersk sold its 75% stake in Esvagt, which operates ships that service offshore oil rigs and clean up oil spills, to investment firms 3i Infrastructure and AMP Capital
BY By Robbie Whelan
WC 242 words
PD 7 July 2015
ET 13:47
SN The Wall Street Journal Online
SC WSJO
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Dow Jones & Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

A.P. Møller-Mærsk A/S has sold its majority stake in Esvagt, a shipping company that operates offshore service and rescue vessels, to two infrastructure investment firms from the U.K. and Australia, for $610 million.

The deal is the latest in a series of divestments made by the Danish conglomerate in order to focus on its core businesses of container shipping and oil exploration. The company has sold off assets worth billions of dollars over the last few years, including tankers that carry liquefied natural gas and a large stake in the lender Danske Bank. Maersk has also invested in oil-drilling equipment, marine terminals and mega-container ships.

TD 

ESVAGT, founded in 1981, owns a fleet of 43 vessels that provide emergency response services for offshore oil rigs, help clean up oil spills, and assist in moving rigs, tankers and workers to and from offshore oil projects. Maersk accumulated a 75% stake in the company in the 1990s.

The buyers were 3i Infrastructure Plc, a British firm that invests in energy projects across Europe, and AMP Capital, an Australian infrastructure investment fund with $124 billion in assets under management.

Write to Robbie Whelan at robbie.whelan@wsj.com[mailto:robbie.whelan@wsj.com]

HD Press Release: Fagron NV: Disclosure of received notification
WC 428 words
PD 20 July 2015
ET 01:01
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

   Regulated information 
 
   Waregem (Belgium)/Rotterdam (Netherlands)(1) , 20 July 2015 
 
   Pursuant to the Belgian law of 2 May 2007 regarding the disclosure of 
major shareholdings in listed companies, Fagron received a notification 
on 17 July 2015 from Danske Bank concerning the acquisition of voting 
securities. The shareholding of Danske Bank crossed the disclosure 
threshold of 3% through the acquisition of voting securities. 
 
   Based on the denominator of 31,667,794 (total number of voting rights) 
and the latest received notifications, the major shareholders of Fagron 
are: 
 
 
 
 
                                Number of shares  % of effective voting rights 
Carmignac Gestion                      2,463,267                         7.78% 
TIAA-CREF Asset Management LLC         1,635,681                         5.17% 
BNP Paribas Investment 
 Partners SA                           1,609,182                         5.08% 
Fidelity Management and 
 Research (FMR LLC)                    1,517,822                         4.79% 
Danske Bank                              984,675                         3.11% 
 
 
   The original notification forms are available on the website 
investors.fagron.com. 
 
   Fagron profile 
 
   Fagron is an innovative scientific pharmaceutical R&D company that is 
focused on optimizing and innovating pharmaceutical compounding. Fagron 
offers Fagron Compounding Services, Fagron Trademarks and Fagron 
Compounding Essentials to pharmacies, hospitals and patients in 32 
countries worldwide. Pharmaceutical compounding is an essential part of 
pharmaceutical care that enables prescribers and pharmacists to fulfil 
the worldwide growing need for tailor-made medication. Fagron's own R&D 
department consists of 45 researchers and more than 300 pharmacists who 
are working continually on developing new concepts, vehicles and 
formulations to treat an increasing number of patients with tailor-made 
compounded medication. 
 
   The Belgian company Fagron NV is located in Waregem and is listed on 
Euronext Brussels and Euronext Amsterdam. The operational activities of 
Fagron are driven by the Dutch company Fagron BV. The head office of 
Fagron BV is located in Rotterdam. 
 
   For further information

   Global Investor Relations Director 
 
   Tel. +31 88 33 11 213

   investors.fagron.com http://investors.fagron.com/[http://investors.fagron.com/]

HD EARNINGS POLL-Danske Bank Q2 pretax profit seen down 2.9 pct
WC 773 words
PD 20 July 2015
ET 04:11
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

TD 

 * Danske Bank Q2 results
    * Due on July 22 at 0600 GMT

    COPENHAGEN, July 20 (Reuters) - Following is a summary of analyst estimates
for the results of Danish bank Danske Bank for the second quarter of
2015, and full years 2015, 2016 and 2017.
    Pretax profit is seen down by 2.9 percent while net profit is expected to
fall by 10.5 percent primarily due to lower trading and insurance income.
       
    (All figures in millions of Danish crowns, except earnings per share,
dividend and target share price in crowns).

HD Press Release: Danske Bank Oyj: Interim Report January-June 2015
WC 1253 words
PD 22 July 2015
ET 02:30
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

Danske Bank Plc Group's Interim Report January-June 2015  July 22, 2015 
 
   Risto Tornivaara, CEO: Pleasing development in credit and deposit 
portfolios in difficult market conditions 
 
   "The operating environment continued to be very challenging during the 
first half-year. Interest rates remained exceptionally low, and the 
Greek crisis increased uncertainty in the financial market. Danske Bank 
Plc Group, the Finnish subsidiary of the Danske Bank A/S Group, was able 
to improve its result in the challenging operating environment. The 
profit before taxes for the first half-year was EUR 113 million, which 
is 9 per cent more than in the same period of 2014. The positive profit 
performance was due to our determined efforts to improve the bank's cost 
structure and the reduction of loan impairment charges. 
 
   Our cost-to-income ratio improved by 2 percentage points on the previous 
year and was 60.5 per cent. The interest rate environment had a negative 
impact on our net interest income, which declined by 2 per cent. Net fee 
income was almost at previous year's level. Operating income totaled EUR 
293 million in January-June, which is 3 per cent less than a year 
earlier. 
 
   Danske Bank's objective is to be the most trusted banking partner for 
Finns. Customer satisfaction improved in all our business units, 
especially among our medium-sized and large corporate customers. Our 
customers' trust was reflected in the development of our credit and 
deposit portfolios in both Personal and Business Banking, which is very 
pleasing, especially considering the difficult market conditions. 
 
   The number of new housing loans grew by over 20 per cent on the previous 
year, boosted by our campaigns focusing on effortless banking. More than 
22,000 of our household customers utilised the opportunity to have an 
interest-only period on their home loans, which released some EUR 110 
million in assets for households to use. 
 
   After a long downturn, there are positive signs regarding Finnish 
companies' willingness to invest. The corporate bond market has been 
utilised actively in financing, and there have also been new listings on 
the stock market after a long hiatus. The first half-year was successful 
for Danske Bank's Corporate Finance business: we were chosen to 
participate in arranging the largest IPOs since 2006, and we played a 
key role in several major financing arrangements. 
 
   Danske Bank Plc Group's capital adequacy is very strong, and our capital 
adequacy ratio was 15.5 per cent (14.5% at the end of 2014) at the end 
of the period. Our aim is to grow in Finland, and our strong capital 
adequacy provides a good foundation for this."

   Events after the reporting period 
 
   Financial Supervisory Authority (FIN-FSA) has, in their press release on 
6(th) July 2015, designated Danske Bank Plc as systemically important 
credit institution (O-SII) in Finland in accordance with the Act on 
Credit Institutions. At the same time FIN-FSA imposed an additional 
capital requirement of 0.5 per cent, which has to be covered by Common 
Equity Tier 1 capital (CET1 capital). The new requirement must be 
fulfilled as of 7(th) January 2016. 
 
   In July 2015 Danske Bank Plc also received the Finnish FSA's approval to 
use the F-IRB approach for calculating credit Risk Exposure amount (REA) 
for the asset class corporate in Finland. The approval will be 
implemented during Q3 2015. 
 
   Outlook for 2015 
 
   Growth in Finnish economy is expected to remain on a very modest level 
also during the rest of the year 2015 and mainly driven by growth in 
exports to Western markets and USA. 
 
   Lending to personal and corporate customers is expected to continue a 
slight increase also during the rest of the year. However, due to the 
low domestic demand, relatively quiet activity on the housing markets 
and continuing low level of interest rates, we expect the net interest 
income and total income to decrease slightly compared to the previous 
year. 
 
   Expenses are expected to be lowered compared to previous year as we 
continue to have a strong focus on improving our cost efficiency and 
operational processes during the second half of 2015. Overall, we expect 
that our profit before loan impairment charges for 2015 will be slightly 
better than 2014. 
 
   Impairment charges are expected to in broadly line with 2014 thus net 
profit is expected to be at the same level as 2014. 
 
   This guidance is generally subject to uncertainty and depends on 
economic conditions. Our trading income and loan loss charges are 
particularly uncertain.

HD Danske Bank Lifts Guidance as Second-Quarter Net Profit Beats
BY By Dominic Chopping
WC 337 words
PD 22 July 2015
ET 03:06
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Denmark's biggest lender, Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO), Wednesday lifted full-year guidance as higher customer activity, improving macroeconomic conditions and lower impairments helped drive a better-than-expected 6% rise in second quarter net profit.

TD 

For 2015, the bank now expects a net profit above 16 billion Danish kroner ($2.35 billion), having previously guided for a figure above DKK14 billion. Total income is now expected to increase from 2014 levels while impairment charges in its core activities will decline to a level significantly below 2014, it said.

Net profit at the Copenhagen-based bank rose to DKK4.31 billion in the three months to June 30, up from DKK4.07 billion in the year-earlier period and above an average DKK3.67 billion forecast by analysts in a FactSet poll.

Danish and Swedish central banks earlier this year sent interest rates into negative territory to keep their currencies from getting stronger, and Danske Bank said that this prevailing interest rate environment with very low deposit margins has put its net interest income under pressure. However, quarterly net interest income increased slightly to DKK8.63 billion from DKK8.4 billion, after seeing increased returns from its bond portfolio and higher lending volumes.

Net fee income increased 17% as many of its customers refinanced their mortgages to take advantage of the historically low interest rates, it said. Trading income also increased, with customer activity increasing amid volatile financial markets.

Loan impairments swung from a charge of DKK626 million in the second quarter of last year to a reversal of DKK219 million this year.

Danske said its common equity Tier 1 capital ratio--a measure of financial strength--stood at 14.3% at the end of the quarter, just down from the 14.4% a year ago.

-Write to Dominic Chopping at dominic.chopping@wsj.com; Twitter: @WSJNordics

(END) Dow Jones Newswires

July 22, 2015 03:06 ET (07:06 GMT)

HD Danske Bank nets EUR 12.8 mln in Estonia in H1
WC 324 words
PD 22 July 2015
ET 03:26
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Jul 22, BNS – The Estonian unit of Danske Bank earned a net profit of 12.8 million euros in the first half of 2015 compared to 18.9 million euros a year earlier.

The decrease was mainly a result of smaller income from financial transactions and a decline in service fees, CEO Aivar Rehe said. The cost to revenue ratio was 42 percent compared to the year-earlier 35 percent.

TD 

Net interest income totaled 11 million euros and income from service fees 5.9 million euros. The corresponding figures a year ago were 10.8 million and 7.6 million euros. Net profit from financial transactions was three million euros compared to 4.8 million euros the year before.

"The bank offers actively loan and settlement products to local and international businesses and the public sector. Business volumes in the corporate customer segment increased in the first half of the year thanks to competitive loan offers," Rehe said.

The corporate loan portfolio increased by 112 million euros or 23 percent in annual comparison, totaling 606 million euros at the end of June. The bank's share of the corporate loan market is 6.2 percent, up by 1 percent year on year.

At the end of June deposits exceeded loans by 1.11 billion euros. A year earlier the difference was 1.15 billion euros. The loan to deposit ratio was 38.6 percent compared to the year-earlier 33.8 percent.

"At the beginning of this year Danske Bank announced its decision to reposition its business activities in the Baltic states to concentrate on servicing corporate and private banking customers. These two customer segments will comprise the bank's core activities, and in presenting our financial results, we shall concentrate on the results of these activities," Rehe said.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8821, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD Danske Bank’s net profit in Lithuania grows 8 pct in H1 y/y
WC 204 words
PD 22 July 2015
ET 04:30
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Jul 22, BNS - The Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, reported 7.8 million euros in unaudited net profit for the first half of this year, a rise of 8.3 percent from the year-earlier figure of 7.2 million euros.

Pretax profit from core operations fell by an annual 12.1 percent to 9.4 million euros, the branch said in its interim report.

TD 

“Business and private banking services are the strategic goal of Danske Bank group in the Baltic countries hence we will further consolidate our positions in these segments in the second half of the year,” the branch’s CEO, Gintautas Galvanauskas, said in a press release.

Successful refocusing of Lithuania’s exports to the European Union’s (EU) countries and positive business expectations let expect a moderate growth in lending this year, he added.

The branch’s loan portfolio shrank by 5.9 percent in the reporting period to 511 million euros. Its deposit portfolio grew by 2.5 percent to 856 million euros.

HD ''Danske Bank'' in Latvia posts EUR 0.46 million in six-month profit
BY Airisa Âdamsone
WC 422 words
PD 22 July 2015
ET 04:47
SN Latvian News Agency
SC LETA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 LETA .

LP 

RIGA, July 22 (LETA) - ''Danske Bank'' in Latvia operated with EUR 464,000 in net-profit in the first six months of the year.The bank posted EUR 0.97 million in profit before impairment charges, ''Danske Bank'' informs.With growing business volume, the bank’s total income from core activities reached EUR 3.8 million, an increase of 16 percent. Net interest income grew 57 percent to EUR 2.6 million, while net fee income grew 32 percent to EUR 1.1 million.Meanwhile, the bank’s expenses grew 30 percent because of investments in a shared IT platform for operations in Latvia, Estonia and Lithuania. The platform will allow ''Danske Bank'' to ensure sophisticated and uniform offerings for corporate customers with business needs in the Baltic countries. It is scheduled for implementation by the end of 2016.

TD 

In addition, the bank also increased slightly the number of employees serving its growing business customer base.The bank’s core activity deposit portfolio grew 21 percent to EUR 206.4 million. While the market for business lending in Latvia is showing the first signs of growth, the bank expanded its loan portfolio for core segment customers by 36 percent in the past 12 months to EUR 248.4 million at the end of June 2015. The business loan portfolio rose 35 percent to EUR 243 million. ''Danske Bank'' points out that it is committed to continuing to increase its business banking market share in Latvia by offering customers sophisticated advice and tailor-made financing solutions.“The current business environment has presented many challenges for Latvian companies,” says Raivis Kakanis, CEO of ''Danske Bank'' in Latvia. “But despite the obstacles of export sanctions and the unstable geopolitical situation, the Latvian economy grew 1.9 percent in the first quarter, and we expect that growth will pick up in the second half of 2015. A positive factor that demonstrates the flexibility of Latvian exporting companies is the resilience of Latvian exports of goods and services. In the first quarter, they grew 2.7 percent year-on-year.”“Despite the vulnerable business environment that forces companies to be cautious in considering new financial liabilities, our focused efforts have produced a solid 35 percent growth in business lending. We are committed to continuing to strengthen our business banking position going forward,'' he added.''Dansk Bank'' in Latvia operates one branch at the moment and employs a staff of 80 persons.

HD Latvian branch of Danske Bank posts EUR 464,000 profit for H1
WC 321 words
PD 22 July 2015
ET 05:40
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Jul 22, BNS - The Latvian branch of Danske Bank closed the first Half of 2015 with a 464,000 euros profit, down 2.3 times from the same period a year ago, the bank's spokeswoman Ieva Zauere told BNS.

She said that revenues from the branches core activities in the said period came to 3.758 million euros, up 16 percent from the first half of 2014, while expenses rose by 30 percent to 2.793 million euros.

TD 

Zauere said that expenses rose mainly because of investments in an IT platform that is common for branches in Latvia, Lithuania and Estonia. The common IT platform will be introduced by the end of 2016. The bank has also increased the number of employees to ensure quality service for the growing number of corporate customers.

Thus, the profit before provisions of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank reaches 965,000 euros, down 11 percent from a year ago. The provisions, meanwhile came to 501,000 euros in the first six months of this year.

"Despite the unstable business environment, making companies be carefull in assessment of new financial liabilities, we have achieved a 35 percent growth in business lending. We have resolved to strengthen our position in the corporate customer segment also in the future, said Raivis Kakanis, the head of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank in late June has issued 248.425 million euros in loans, up 36 percent from a year ago, and had attracted 206.351 million euros in deposits, up 21 percent.

In the first half of 2014 the Latvian branch of Danske Bank earned 1.081 million euros in profit.

The Latvian branch of  Danske Bank became part of the Danish Danske Bank Group in 2007.

Riga newsroom, +371 6708 8606, eko_zinas@ bns.lv

SE Finance
HD Recovering economy reduces loan losses at Danske Bank
WC 144 words
PD 23 July 2015
SN The Irish Times
SC IRTI
PG 3
LA English
CY (c) 2015, The Irish Times.

LP 

Danske Bank raised its full-year forecast after profit in the second quarter climbed as a recovering economy helped reduce loan losses.

The bank also said it would start treating its operations in Northern Ireland as a "standalone business unit" and no longer include it in its personal banking and business banking.

TD 

"We have made a business review that concluded that synergies between the Northern Irish market and the Nordic markets are limited," Danske said.

Denmark's biggest bank said it expects net income to exceed 16 billion kroner (€2.1 billion) this year, about 2 billion kroner more than it had previously estimated.

Net income rose 8 per cent to 4.5 billion kroner in the three months through June, beating the average 3.8 billion-krone estimate of analysts surveyed.

- (Additional reporting: Bloomberg)

SE News
HD Sale speculation as Danske makes North a standalone operation
BY Colm Kelpie
WC 323 words
PD 23 July 2015
SN Irish Independent
SC IINM
ED 1; National
PG 3
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Independent Newspapers Ireland Ltd

LP 

DANSKE Bank's Northern Ireland operations will become a standalone business unit instead of part of the Danish giant's personal banking and business banking.

The move takes effect from January and Danske Bank Northern Ireland will be disclosed in financial statements as a separate business unit. Danske announced in late 2013 that it was shutting the bulk of its banking operations in the Republic. Danske's Northern Ireland wing recorded a pre-tax profit for the first six months of the year of £65m, a big improvement on last year.

TD 

"The first half of the year has been a particularly strong one for Business Banking. We have already provided more new lending to business customers in 2015 than we did in the whole of 2014," said Danske UK chief executive Gerry Mallon.

"This is down to an encouraging increase in demand for lending from our existing customers after a long spell of relatively subdued demand and the continued acquisition of new to bank customers." Danske said it would be introducing a new operating model for the North.

"Our activities in Northern Ireland will operate as a standalone business unit rather than as part of Personal Banking and Business Banking," Danske said. "We have made a business review that concluded that synergies between the Northern Irish market and the Nordic markets are limited, and we are confident that the change will better enable us to create value for our customers in Northern Ireland, to develop our market position and to improve profitability."

The move sparked speculation that the Northern Ireland operations were being primed for sale. "They are making the bank in Northern Ireland ready to be sold and it makes good sense," analyst Christian Hede from Nordea Markets said.

In response, A Danske spokesman said: "We are happy with our activities in Northern Ireland and have no plans to sell."

HD Danske Bank grants EUR 4.9mn for Vilnius District Municipality's projects
WC 145 words
PD 23 July 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, July 23 (ELTA) - Lithuanian subsidiary of Danske Bank and Vilnius District Municipality have signed a four-year EUR 4.87 million financing agreement. Additional funds will allow the municipality to implement investment projects.

According to Algirdas Vilys, Head of Danske Bank Customer Service Centre in Vilnius, Danske Bank's proposal submitted for a public tender was the best one.

TD 

Mayor of Vilnius District Municipality, Marija Rekst, said the funds would be used to create the infrastructure of social care establishments, renovate or expand water supply and wastewater networks, renovate education establishments and for other public infrastructure projects.

Danske Bank is the second-largest bank by assets in the Nordic countries. Danske Bank Group operates in 15 countries, its shareholders' equity at the end of 2014 totalled EUR 20.6 billion.

HD Danske Bank analyst: Lithuanian corporate sector’s growth to be moderate in H2
WC 248 words
PD 27 July 2015
ET 04:07
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Jul 27, BNS - Improvements in business expectations show that Lithuania’s companies have adjusted to geopolitical changes and resumed planning of expansion, an analyst of Danske Bank has said, adding that the growth will still remain moderate in the second half of the year.

“Although the capacity utilization remains record high, thus far, this factor has not pointed to a potential rebound of investment in business this year. There are signs that businesses, which had surplus production capacities in the post-crisis period, are very responsible in their assessment of new investment today,” Dinas Petrikas, the director of Corporate Banking Division at the Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank, said in a press release.

TD 

Businesses had already adjusted to the current geopolitical situation and were likely to invest the amounts necessary for growth, provided that the geopolitical situation remained unchanged, he said.

“A new phase of the European Union’s support may encourage some companies to increase investment. Still, the companies, which will not receive such support, are not likely to implement larger investment. With the lessons of the financial crisis still fresh in the memory, businesses are still wary of raising debts too much,” the analyst said.

In Petrikas’ view, if the geopolitical situation and the health of export markets remain unchanged, the performance of Lithuania’s companies should become positive next year.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8521

OSLO, Aug 4 (Reuters) - The Norwegian purchasing managers' index (PMI) rose to 45.8 points on a seasonally adjusted basis in July from an upwardly revised 44.2 points in June, data from logistics association NIMA and Danske Bank showed on Tuesday.

   Fagron profile 
 
   Fagron is a scientific pharmaceutical R&D company that is focused on 
optimizing and innovating customized pharmaceutical care. Fagron 
provides Fagron Specialty Pharma Services, Fagron Trademarks and Fagron 
Essentials to pharmacies, clinics and hospitals in 32 countries 
worldwide. 
 
   The Belgian company Fagron NV is located in Waregem and is listed on 
Euronext Brussels and Euronext Amsterdam. The operational activities of 
Fagron are driven by the Dutch company Fagron BV. The head office of 
Fagron BV is located in Rotterdam.

HD EARNINGS POLL-Finland's Sampo seen set to lift 2015 profitability view
WC 1080 words
PD 11 August 2015
ET 09:42
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

TD 

 * Sampo seen likely to lift its 2015 P&C profitability outlook
    * Q2 results due on Wednesday, August 12 around 0630 GMT

    By Jussi Rosendahl
    HELSINKI, Aug 11 (Reuters) - Finnish financial holding company Sampo
 is expected to upgrade the 2015 profitability outlook for its
property and casualty insurance arm following the unit's strong performance in
Sweden, a Reuters poll showed.
    Sampo, due to report its second-quarter results on Wednesday, owns the
biggest Nordic property and casualty (P&C) insurer If. It also owns more than a
fifth of shares in both Nordea, the region's largest lender, and
Topdanmark, a rival insurer from Denmark.
    In May, Sampo set a target range for its full-year P&C combined ratio to
88-91 percent, and analysts in a Reuters poll on average now expect it to come
in at 86.2 percent. A lower figure indicates better profitability.
    "They could specify the range and lower it somewhat," said Jaakko Tyrvainen,
analyst at Evli brokerage, who has 'accumulate' recommendation for the stock.
    "If's underlying profitability in Sweden has been improving for some time
now. Looks like the cooperation with Nordea is bearing fruit. Also, they have a
strong position in Sweden's car insurance market, and we have seen some good car
sales statistics lately."
    In the second-quarter, Sampo is expected to report If's combined ratio at
82.3 percent, but that will be boosted by one-offs.
    Sampo has raised its annual dividend every year since 2008, and analysts
have also lately increased their forecasts on the next few payouts.
    The poll expects Sampo to pay out a dividend of 2.15 euros for 2015, 2.31
euros from 2016 and 2.47 euros from 2017. It paid 1.95 euros from last year.
    Sampo, 12-percent owned by the state of Finland, has for years been sitting
on cash made in successful M&A steps. It sold its banking business to Danske
Bank just before the financial crash, and then bought Nordea shares
at their low price levels of 2008 and 2009.
    The group's solvency ratio stood at 193 percent by end-March, well above the
EU minimum requirement of 100 percent.

HD Aivar Rehe to quit as manager of Danske Bank Estonia
WC 220 words
PD 18 August 2015
ET 02:58
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Aug 18, BNS – Aivar Rehe is about to leave the position of manager of the Estonian branch of Danske Bank A/S from Sept. 1, from which date his duties will be performed by Ivar Pae, head of Baltic banking at Danske Bank.

The bank has launched a search for a new manager.

TD 

Rehe said in a press release the years worked at the bank were full of intensive work and challenges, having included economic and banking crises as well as years of peaceful growth alike. "Now, in a period of repositioning of the bank, it's right to give new people a chance," Rehe said.

Rehe remained tight-lipped when asked by BNS about his plans.

"I wish to thank Aivar for ten years of committed and competent work at Danske Bank. We wish Aivar success in his future activities," Pae, who will take over as acting manager from Sept. 1, said.

Rehe's leaving will bring with it a change also in the management of the Estonian Banking Association, on whose board Rehe will be replaced by Pae.

On the Estonian market Danske Bank Group focuses on corporate customers and individuals related to them.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8815, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD Germany’s Haven Status Enhanced With Bonds Seen Extending Gains
WC 431 words
PD 23 August 2015
ET 09:25
SN Mist News
SC MISTNW
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Misr Information Services and Trading. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

Bloomberg

Germany’s government bonds may extend gains next week as investors seek haven assets after China’s manufacturing activity plunged to a six-year low and an index of commodity prices touched the lowest level since 2002.

TD 

Yields on German 10-year bunds, Europe’s benchmark sovereign securities, fell to their lowest level in more than two months after Greek Prime Minister Alexis Tsipras stepped down to force an early election, clouding the political outlook. The yield premiums, or spreads, that investors get for holding the region’s higher-yielding debt instead of similar-maturity German bunds may increase, according to Danske Bank A/S .

“There has been a lot of risk-averse trading,” said Jens Peter Soerensen, chief analyst at Danske Bank in Copenhagen. “The Greek vote news and the decline in oil and emerging markets has seen spreads widen between peripherals versus core bonds. So where do you prefer to stay? You will stay in bunds.”

Germany’s 10-year bund yields dropped 10 basis points, or 0.1 percentage point, this week to 0.56 percent at the 5 p.m. close in London on Friday, the lowest since June 2. The 1 percent security due August 2025 climbed 0.945, or 9.45 euros per 1,000-euro ($1,136) face amount, to 104.22.

Soerensen said German bund yields “can easily go lower” and, if they breach 0.5 percent, could drop to 0.25 percent in the next one to two months.

Spreads Widen

The yield spread between Italian 10-year securities and German bunds widened to as much as 130 basis points Friday, the most since July 14. Italy’s 10-year bond yield increased five basis points this week to 1.86 percent.

Signs of a deepening slowdown in China’s economy and tumbling commodities stoked deflationary fears, boosting demand for the safest fixed-income securities. Minutes of the Federal Reserve ’s July meeting released Aug. 19 also prompted investors to push back their outlook for interest-rate increases.

“The focus will be on inflation and oil prices and if they continue to trend lower,” Soerensen said.

Investors’ outlook for inflation touched a five-month low this week, with five-year inflation swap rates, a market gauge of consumer-price growth over that period, slipping to 0.73 percent on Aug. 21, the lowest since March 2.

German business confidence fell in August, according to the median forecast in a Bloomberg survey of economists before the report is released on Aug. 25.

HD Falling emerging markets will not have major impact on Lithuania - Danske Bank analyst
WC 627 words
PD 26 August 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, August 26 (ELTA) - Falling stocks in China and other emerging markets will not have a major direct impact on Lithuania, whose export to India, China and the Southeast Asia amounts to less than 1 percent of the total export. What will pose more problems is the decreasing purchasing power in Russia and other countries of the Commonwealth of Independent States. However, cheaper oil will save the situation, says Rokas Grajauskas, Baltic Analyst at Danske Bank.

TD 

It used to be commonly said, "When the United States sneezes, the rest of world catches cold". Now the saying may be applied to China. When China sneezes, all emerging markets catch cold - especially those economies that are tightly related to China, first of all countries of the East and Southeast Asia, such as Indonesia, Malaysia, Taiwan or Singapore. Even a slight slowdown in China's growth may have a painful outcome for the growth of aforementioned economies. This is reflected by the nervous reaction of the financial market.

What happens to China and other emerging markets will depend not only on the market, but on the Chinese government's response. Markets have already reacted positively to the decision of the People's Bank of China to cut its key lending rate by 0.25 percentage points to 4.6 percent.

The impact of falling emerging markets should not be very significant on Lithuania. China is only 26th on the list of Lithuania's export partners. While Lithuania's exports to India, China and all countries of the Southeast Asia account for merely 0.7 percent of its total export.

It should be pointed out that a bigger threat would be if Lithuanian exporters were deterred from expanding in these markets. There is no doubt that difficulties are temporary, while in the medium and long term these markets will still remain one of the fastest growing in the world. Consumption and the middle-class will be on the rise there. Thus export to these markets should be evaluated from the strategic perspective and should not be pushed completely aside.

China is the second largest oil consumer in the world. Therefore China's economic slowdown is the main factor causing oil price decrease at the moment. On the one hand, this is good news for oil-importing countries such as Lithuania. Decreasing oil and fuel prices not only loosen consumers' wallets and contribute to more rapid consumption growth but also have a better effect on competition.

Taking into consideration that energy-intensive sectors of transportation and fertiliser production play an important role in Lithuania's economy, 10 percent lower oil prices account for approximately 0.4 percent of GDP growth.

On the other hand, decreasing oil prices negatively affect economic growth of export partners important to Lithuania - first and foremost Russia and other CIS countries, which recently accounted for nearly a third of Lithuania's total export. As oil prices have slumped to USD 43 per barrel, Russian rouble has jumped to 70 roubles per dollar. Meanwhile, Kazakhstan was forced to devalue its currency by nearly 25 percent. Obviously, as the purchasing power of these countries tumbles, Lithuanian exporters will find it even more difficult to export there. Nevertheless, it should be yet another reason to revise Lithuania's long term export strategy.

As the euro area is finding its feet, there will be more opportunities for Lithuania to export to this crucial market. The first half of 2015 showed that as export to Russia was shrinking, it was counterbalanced by growing export flows to the euro area and Nordic countries. Not only manufacturing industry but service sectors such as transport and tourism are able to reorient.

Karolis Broga

SE MARKETS & INVESTING
HD European banks rush to issue covered bonds; Capital markets
BY By Thomas Hale
WC 394 words
PD 2 September 2015
SN Financial Times
SC FTFTA
ED USA Ed1
PG 18
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

European markets saw a rush of covered bond issuance yesterday as primary market activity proved resilient to global volatility coming from China.

The deals included covered bonds issued by Santander, UniCredit Bank Austria and Danske Bank, which raised a total of €2.5bn. A 10-year €500m bond issued by Commerzbank on Monday met strong demand.

TD 

Covered bonds, an idiosyncrasy of European debt markets, are backed by mortgage assets on banks' balance sheets and are viewed as low-risk investments. The investor has recourse to both the issuing bank and the underlying assets in the event of a default.

Yesterday's issuance, the highest this year, came amid falling global stock markets as jitters over China continued to unnerve investors. Demand for the asset class is supported by European Central Bank purchases under a longstanding bank support programme.

"The general market sentiment is probably not that great, but at least in the covered bond market it's holding up very well," said Joost Beaumont, fixed-income strategist at ABN Amro. "Execution risk was quite high during times of volatility and that has come down significantly, as confirmed by [the] deals."

Markets were expecting significant supply in the coming months, he added.

Volatility in global financial markets - stemming from central bank intervention, Greek negotiations and extreme market movements in China - has been a thorn in the side of primary market activity in recent months, with many issuers reluctant to brave unwelcoming conditions.

In May European bank bond issuance dried up after the 10-year German Bund yield rose sharply. In July Greek fears derailed primary debt market activity .

This week's sharp rise in primary covered bond issuance comes after the ECB increased its purchases of the assets last week through its third covered bond purchase programme. The ECB bought €1.9bn of covered bonds last week, and holds a total portfolio of about €111bn through the third programme.

Investors have complained that ECB intervention is distorting the market , saying the programme dramatically reduces outstanding supply. But according to Mr Beaumont, the demand ensured by the ECB's presence contributed to this week's activity. "It's most positive for issuers," he said. "If you bring a deal, you know the eurosystem is there to absorb part of the deal."

HD *Fitch Affirms Danske Bank and Realkredit Danmark at 'A'/Stable
WC 2024 words
PD 8 September 2015
ET 07:22
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

8 Sep 2015 07:22 ET Press Release: Fitch Affirms Danske Bank and Realkredit Danmark at 'A'/Stable

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings:

TD 

Fitch Ratings-Paris/London-08 September 2015: Fitch Ratings has affirmed Danske Bank's (Danske) and its mortgage bank subsidiary Realkredit Danmark's (Realkredit) Long-term Issuer Default Ratings (IDRs) at 'A' with Stable Outlooks, and their Viability Ratings (VRs) at 'a'. A full list of rating actions is provided at the end of this commentary.

KEY RATING DRIVERS - DANSKE'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- Danske's ratings reflects the bank's strong Danish and, to a lesser extent, Nordic franchise, which provide stable revenue generation across a wide range of products, sound capitalisation as well as healthy funding and liquidity. However, wholesale funding reliance makes the bank sensitive to a loss of investor confidence. The ratings also incorporate a continuous improvement in asset quality and profitability metrics.

Since 2008 Danske's asset quality ratios have been significantly affected by the bank's exposure to Irish real estate, as well as a prolonged downturn in the Danish economy. While the level of impaired loans remains higher than at peers, asset quality has improved in recent years. This should continue, driven by the ongoing wind-down of the Irish portfolio, now classified as non-core, and a recovering Danish economy.

Earnings have also improved, driven primarily by declining loan impairment charges. These used to consume between one-third and three-quarters of pre-impairments profits but are now down to more normalised levels. Negative interest rates in Denmark have had a manageable impact on earnings, being partly offset by mortgage lending re-pricing and volume growth. Fitch expects the bank's risk appetite to remain moderate and that management will remain focused on driving profitability via lower costs and without increasing the bank's risk appetite. Danske has a strong management team, in Fitch's opinion, but senior management turnover has been fairly high in recent years.

-

- Danske has a well-diversified funding base. Similar to most Nordic peers, it has significant reliance on wholesale funding, in particular through its mortgage loan business which by law is exclusively funded through Danish mortgage bonds. Demand for Danish mortgage bonds should remain strong in light of the need from predominantly domestic financial institutions, insurance companies and pension funds to hold highly liquid, high-quality, securities in domestic currency. This is reinforced by the fairly limited outstanding volume of Danish government bonds. Nonetheless, maintaining a significant liquidity portfolio to mitigate refinancing risk is key to Danske's current ratings.

Danske's risk-weighted capital adequacy ratios compare well with those of international peers, but lag behind those of some Nordic peers. Leverage is acceptable in a European context, with tangible common equity/tangible assets at around 4%.

KEY RATING DRIVERS - REALKREDIT'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- Realkredit Danmark's IDRs and VR reflects Fitch's view that profitability, although moderate, will enable the mortgage bank to absorb unexpected shocks in Denmark until economic growth is firmly back on track in the country. Despite the sharing of some services with its parent bank, the ratings of Realkredit Danmark are based on its standalone financial strength. Fitch also expects that capital is, to an extent, fungible between Danske and Realkredit Danmark, and thus the VRs are, to a certain degree, inter-connected.

The ratings reflect the bank's strong Danish franchise as the second-largest mortgage lender, its solid capitalisation and its strong asset quality. Its monoline business model and reliance on wholesale funding constrain the ratings, although risks associated with the latter are mitigated by a large, deep and liquid domestic funding market.

Realkredit Danmark's assets represent the majority of Danske's mortgage loan exposure and Fitch expects the quality of the mortgage lending to remain strong, supported by a stabilising Danish economy. However, profitability should remain modest, driven by its low-margin mortgage loan business.

Realkredit Danmark is by law entirely wholesale-funded, largely through issuance of Danish mortgage bonds. Similar to its domestic peers, about one-third of Realkredit Danmark's bonds mature within a year to match the duration of the bank's underlying mortgage loan. Generally such dependence on short-term wholesale funding would suggest a lower rating. However, the supportive dynamics of the Danish mortgage bond market are an important mitigating factor for this risk. Realkredit Danmark's move to extend bond maturities and Denmark's law on mortgage bond maturity extensions will help reduce refinancing risks (see: 'Nordic Banks' Significant Wholesale Funding Reliance', dated 29 April 2015)

Realkredit Danmark's capital adequacy ratios compare well with those of domestic and international peers. Low risk weights on mortgage loans boost reported capital ratio while leverage is acceptable in a European context.

SUPPORT RATING AND SUPPORT RATING FLOOR

- Danske's and Realkredit's '5' Support Ratings and 'No Floor' Support Rating Floors reflect Fitch's view that senior creditors can no longer rely on receiving full extraordinary support from the sovereign in case of need. In Fitch's view, the EU's Bank Recovery and Resolution Directive (BRRD) is now sufficiently progressed to provide a framework for resolving banks that is likely to require senior creditors participating in losses, if necessary, instead of or ahead of a bank receiving sovereign support.

In the EU, BRRD has been effective in member states since 1 January 2015, including minimum loss absorption requirements before resolution financing or alternative financing (eg, government stabilisation funds) can be used. Full application of BRRD, including the bail-in tool, is required from 1 January 2016.

SUBORDINATED DEBT AND OTHER HYBRID SECURITIES

- Subordinated debt and other hybrid capital issued by Danske are all notched down from the bank's VR and have been affirmed accordingly. The ratings reflect each instrument's respective non-performance and relative loss severity risk profiles, which vary considerably.

Danske's CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 instruments are notched down once below the bank's VR to reflect the notes' higher expected loss severity relative to senior unsecured creditors. The notching also takes into consideration a lack of contractual full write-down or conversion language. .

Fitch rates Danske's other Tier 2 instruments three notches below the VR to reflect loss severity (one notch) and incremental non-performance risk (two notches). Of the latter, Fitch has applied a single notch for incremental non-performance risk to legacy issues because of the issuer's ability to defer coupons. The ability to defer interest is the differentiation between the old-style Tier 2 instruments and the new CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 notes.

Hybrid Tier 1 securities are rated four notches below Danske's VR to reflect the higher-than- average loss severity risk of these securities (two notches) as well as their high risk of non-performance (an additional two notches).

Danske's Additional Tier 1 instruments are rated five notches below Danske's VR, reflecting the notes' higher expected loss severity relative to senior unsecured creditors (two notches) and higher non-performance risk (three notches), given their fully discretionary coupon payments. Fitch believes Danske's capital buffer being above the 7% CET1 trigger and the minimal capital ratio taking into account the additional buffer on Danish systemically important financial institutions is sufficient to limit the notching for non-performance risk to three (which could otherwise result in wider notching).

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- DANSKE'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- The Stable Outlook incorporates Fitch's expectation that Danske will continue to improve profitability while gradually reducing its volume of impaired loans both in Denmark as well as in its non-core business.

An upgrade is currently unlikely given the current earnings and asset quality pressures. Over the medium- to long-term, an upgrade is contingent on the bank successfully executing its current strategy, with a clear focus on home markets. This is provided that asset quality metrics also continue to improve, combined with sustainable and solid internal capital generation.

The ratings could be downgraded if Danske is unable to competitively access wholesale funding markets, if its Danish business faces a significant deterioration in asset quality that materially affects its capitalisation or if its improving earnings trend reverses, reducing its ability to absorb shocks.

REALKREDIT'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- The Stable Outlook reflects Fitch's view that Realkredit Danmark will maintain its focus on asset quality, will continue to generate capital internally and that its adequate earnings will be able to absorb unexpected shocks.

A rating downgrade would most likely be a result of Realkredit Danmark being unable to competitively access wholesale funding markets or if it significantly increases its reliance on international debt investors who may prove less stable during financial stress. A downgrade of Danske's ratings, or reduced focus on liquidity, would also be rating-negative.

An upgrade is currently unlikely given the bank's already high ratings and monoline business model.

SUPPORT RATING AND SUPPORT RATING FLOOR

- An upgrade to the Support Ratings and upward revision to the Support Rating Floors would be contingent on a positive change in Denmark's propensity to support its banks. While not impossible, this is highly unlikely in Fitch's view.

SUBORDINATED DEBT AND OTHER HYBRID SECURITIES

- The ratings of the subordinated debt and other hybrid capital issued by Danske are sensitive to a change in Danske's VR.

The rating actions are as follows:

Danske Bank

- Long-term IDR: affirmed at 'A', Outlook Stable

- Short-term IDR: affirmed at 'F1'

HD Danske Bank names new heads of corporate finance
WC 152 words
PD 10 September 2015
ET 08:02
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Sept 10 (Reuters) - Danske Bank has appointed Christian Blinkenberg and Christian Lindholm as co-heads of its Danish corporate finance unit.

Blinkenberg, 41, came to Danske Bank in 2013 from investment bank Goldman Sachs in London and will focus on mergers and acquisitions (M&A).

TD 

Lindholm, 44, has been working for Danske Bank for the last 15 years and will concentrate on equity capital markets (ECM) in his new position. The two men replace Jesper H. Hansen, who left the bank nine months ago.

"Christian Blinkenberg and Christian Lindholm have extensive experience within corporate finance and they have played an important role in the higher activity we have seen in the last 12 months," Jens Petter Olsen, head of Danske Bank Capital Markets, said in a statement. (Reporting by Ole Mikkelsen; Editing by Mark Heinrich)

HD ELTEL: Eltel signs a EUR 100 million Finnish domestic commercial paper program
WC 274 words
PD 10 September 2015
ET 11:30
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

Eltel AB has signed a EUR 100 million Finnish domestic commercial paper 
program, which facilitates issuance of commercial papers with tenors 
less than one year for working capital and other short term funding 
purposes. The program also diversifies Eltel's financing capacity. 
The arranger banks are Danske Bank Oyj, Skandinaviska Enskilda Banken AB 
(publ) Helsinki Branch and Swedbank AB Finnish Branch. 
 
For more information, please contact 
Gunilla Wikman, Investor Relations Manager at Eltel AB 
Tel: +46 725 843 630, gunilla.wikman@eltelnetworks.se 
 
About Eltel 
Eltel is a leading European provider of technical services for critical 
infrastructure networks - Infranets - in the segments of Power, 
Communication and Transport & Security, with operations throughout the 
Nordic and Baltic regions, Poland, Germany, the United Kingdom and 
Africa. Eltel provides a broad and integrated range of services, 
spanning from maintenance and upgrade services to project deliveries. 
Eltel has a diverse contract portfolio and a loyal and growing customer 
base of large network owners. The number of employees is approximately 
8,600 and in 2014, Eltel net sales amounted to EUR 1,242 million. 
Eltel's share is listed on Nasdaq Stockholm since February 2015.

HD Press Release: S&P Rates Danish Insurer Danica 'A-'; Outlook Stable
WC 1929 words
PD 11 September 2015
ET 11:47
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
 
The following is a press release from Standard & Poor's: 
 
OVERVIEW 
     -- In our view, Danica Pension Livsforsikringsaktieselskab (Danica) plays 
an important role in Danske Bank's strategy to fortify its position as a 
leading player in Denmark's financial services market. 
     -- We therefore view Danica as core to Danske Bank, but we consider that 
Danica is unlikely to benefit from Danske Bank's additional loss-absorbing 
capacity. 
     -- We are assigning our 'A-' ratings to Danica. 
     -- The stable outlook reflects that on Danske Bank and our expectation 
that Danske Bank's key credit metrics and Danica's strategic role within the 
group will remain stable over the next two years. 
 
STOCKHOLM (Standard & Poor's) Sept. 11, 2015--Standard & Poor's Ratings 
Services said today that it had assigned its 'A-' long-term counterparty 
credit and insurer financial strength ratings to Denmark-based life insurer 
Danica Pension Livsforsikringsaktieselskab (Danica). The outlook is stable. 
 
The ratings reflect our view of Danica as a core operating entity of Danske 
Bank A/S (A/Stable/A-1), reflecting its key role in Danske Bank's financial 
services offering as a market-leading life insurer in Denmark, its strong 
integration within the group, strong although volatile earnings, and gradually 
improving risk profile. 
 
The ratings also reflect our view that, as an insurance subsidiary of Danske 
Bank, Danica would not benefit from additional loss absorbing capacity (ALAC) 
at the bank. We expect that any eventual resolution of Danica would be 
separate from that of the bank, meaning that any outstanding ALAC instruments 
at Danske Bank would not be available for the insurance operations. Therefore, 
we rate Danica at the level of our 'a-' unsupported group credit profile 
assessment on Danske Bank. 
 
Danica is one of the leading life insurers in Denmark, ranking second in terms 
of gross premiums written, with developing insurance operations in Sweden and 
Norway. Danica is also the main life insurance risk carrier within the Danske 
Bank group. In our view, Danica plays a core role in Danske Bank's strategy to 
fortify its position as a leading and well-diversified player in Denmark's 
financial services market. Danica's life and pensions operation is one of 
Danske Bank's five main business lines. 
 
Furthermore, Danica provides Danske Bank with strong, although volatile, 
profits. Danica's profits constituted about 30% of Danske Bank's total profits 
before tax in 2014 (11% after adjustments for a goodwill write-off at Danske 
Bank and a change in accounting at Danica) and 23% on average between 2010 and 
2014, enhancing the bank's income diversification. 
 
We expect that Danica will continue to contribute to Danske Bank's net result 
and that the quality of its earnings will improve as it shifts to unit-linked 
business from traditional policies with guarantees. In 2014, Danica's 
technical provisions for unit-linked business increased to 44% of total 
technical provisions of Danish krone 315 billion (about EUR42 billion), from 20% 
in 2009. We expect the ongoing shift toward less-capital-intensive products 
will gradually strengthen Danica's financial risk profile in the current 
low-yield environment. 
 
In our view, Danica is further leveraging the opportunities of being part of 
the Danske Bank group by increasing its focus on personal customers and small 
and midsize enterprises. Danske Bank is enhancing the product offering at its 
Personal Banking and Business Banking divisions, which we expect will benefit 
Danica. Distribution of insurance products through Danske Bank's branches has 
increased in recent years and represents about 20%-25% of Danica's sales. We 
expect sales through this channel will stay at least at the current level, 
with Danske Bank's branches remaining an important part of Danica's 
distribution strategy. 
 
Danica shares central functions with Danske Bank, with which it also manages 
risk and defines its risk appetite. In addition, Danske Capital, the group's 
asset manager, manages about 70% of Danica's assets relating to traditional 
insurance business with guarantees. 
 
We believe Danske Bank is highly committed to Danica. Danske Bank has not 
needed to financially support Danica since it acquired it in 1995, but has 
backed the insurer's growth. We expect that Danske Bank will support Danica if 
needed, although we don't currently foresee any need for a capital injection. 
We forecast that Danica's regulatory risk-based solvency will remain well 
above the minimum requirements. 
 
The stable outlook on Danica reflects that on Danske Bank, based on Danica's 
core status, and our expectation that Danske Bank's key credit metrics will 
remain stable over the next two years. 
 
We could raise the ratings on Danica over the next 12 to 24 months if we 
revised our assessment of Danske Bank's stand-alone credit profile (SACP) 
upward. Although we do not anticipate an improvement to Danske Bank's SACP at 
present, we see potential for the bank to achieve strong capital and earnings 
over time. 
 
We could lower the ratings on Danica over the next 12 to 24 months if we no 
longer regarded Danica as core to Danske Bank. We consider this unlikely, but 
it could result from a significant weakening of Danica's operating performance 
or group integration, or indications of a reduced commitment from Danske Bank 
to Danica. 
 
RELATED CRITERIA AND RESEARCH

     -- Group Rating Methodology, Nov. 19, 2013

Related research

Support And Additional Loss-Absorbing Capacity, July 13, 2015 
     -- Denmark's Life Insurance Sector Carries An Intermediate Industry And 
Country Risk Assessment, June 2, 2015

HD Estonia: Tartu to place EUR 10.9 mln bonds
WC 136 words
PD 15 September 2015
ET 08:03
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Sep 15, BNS – The city of Tartu is set to place bonds worth up to 10.9 million euros to raise money for investment needs in 2015.

The debt will have a maturity of ten years, it appears from an order of the city government.

TD 

The city will conclude an agreement with the Estonian branch of Danske Bank A/S to organize the placement.

Under the budget of Tartu for 2015, investments of the city are to total 25.3 million euros, 12.4 million euros less than in 2014. Of the money to be invested, budgetary funds make up 12.3 million euros or 49 percent and bridge financing 13 million euros.

HD Swedbank: Swedbank to acquire Danske Bank's retail banking business in Lithuania and Latvia

SC DJDN
LA English

LP 

TD 

 
Swedbank strengthens its footprint in the Baltics by an agreement with 
Danske Bank to acquire its retail banking business in Lithuania and 
Latvia. 
The acquisition affects around 120 000 private customers in Lithuania 
with approximately EUR 525m of loans and 7 000 private customers in 
Latvia with approximately EUR 116m of loans. 
 
- I welcome all new customers and feel confident that they will 
appreciate Swedbank's availability and wide range of digital services. 
We aim to make them as satisfied as the rest of our Baltic customers, 
says Priit Perens, Head of Baltic Banking, Swedbank. 
 
The transaction is subject to approval from the regulatory authorities 
in both Lithuania and Latvia, and will become effective once approved in 
both countries. The acquisition is targeted for closing in the first 
quarter of 2016. 
 
Swedbank AB (publ) is required to disclose this information pursuant to 
the Swedish Securities Markets Act (2007:528), the Swedish Financial 
Instruments Trading Act (1991:980) and/or the regulatory framework of 
Nasdaq Stockholm). This information was sent to be published on 23 
September at 10.00 CET. 
For further information please contact:

38 or gregori.karamouzis@swedbank.com 
Claes Warrén, Press Officer, Swedbank, +46 703 75 00 54 
Swedbank promotes a sound and sustainable financial situation for the 
many people, households and companies. Our vision is to contribute to 
development "Beyond Financial Growth". As a leading bank in the home 
markets of Sweden, Estonia, Latvia and Lithuania, Swedbank offers a wide 
range of financial services and products. Swedbank has over 7 million 
retail customers and around 600 000 corporate customers and 
organisations with 296 branches in Sweden and 149 branches in the Baltic 
countries. The group is also present in other Nordic countries, the US 
and China. 
As of 30 June 2015 the group had total assets of SEK 2 299 billion. Read 
more at www.swedbank.com[http://www.swedbank.com]

HD "Danske Bank" personal customer business in Latvia and Lithuania to be handed over to "Swedbank"
BY Airisa Âdamsone
WC 376 words
PD 23 September 2015
ET 04:57
SN Latvian News Agency
SC LETA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 LETA .

LP 

RIGA, Sept 23 (LETA) - "Danske Bank" has signed a deal with "Swedbank" in Latvia and Lithuania on handing over its personal customer business to "Swedbank".All "Danske Bank" private customers, their accounts, loans, deposits, bankcards, and securities in Latvia and Lithuania will be transferred to "Swedbank". In the near future, the two banks will turn to the banking supervisory authorities in both countries to clear the deal, as "Danske Bank" said in a statement to the media.The deal will concern approximately 7,000 private customers of "Danske Bank" in Latvia and 120,000 in Lithuania.

TD 

The amount of loans transferred from "Danske Bank" to "Swedbank" is approximately EUR 116 million in Latvia and EUR 525 million in Lithuania.As soon as the banks' deal is approved by banking supervisory authorities in both countries, customers will receive detailed information about the transfer process and how it will affect the banking services they currently use."Danske Bank" announced at the beginning of the year that it would concentrate on corporate customers in the three Baltic countries, and gradually exit the personal customer business."Danske Bank" is the largest bank in Denmark. The bank's branch in Latvia focuses on corporate customers.As reported, "Danske Bank" in Latvia operated with EUR 464,000 in net profit in the first six months of the year. The bank's core activity deposit portfolio grew 21 percent to EUR 206.4 million. The bank expanded its loan portfolio for core segment customers to EUR 248.4 million at the end of June, while the business loan portfolio rose to EUR 243 million.According to the Association of Commercial Banks of Latvia, "Danske Bank" branch in Latvia had 3,889 active customers at the end of June, including 3,157 private individuals and 732 legal entities. "Swedbank" had 949,022 active customers at the end of June, including 877,913 private individuals and 71,109 legal entities.At the end of June, "Swedbank" was the largest bank in Latvia in terms of assets, worth EUR 5.15 billion. The Latvian branch of "Danske Bank" was ranked 14th with assets worth EUR 526.7 million.

HD Danske Bank sells Latvian, Lithuanian retail banking business to Swedbank
WC 402 words
PD 23 September 2015
ET 05:09
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Sep 23, BNS - Danske Bank has concluded a deal with Swedbank Lithuania and Swdbank Latvia to sell its retail banking business to Swedbank, BNS was told at the bank.

Danske Bank spokeswoman Ieva Zauere told BNS that the deal affects individual clients' (except for private banking clients) accounts, loans, deposits, payment cards and securities. Documents will soon be submitted to the banking regulators in both countries, asking for permission to close the deal.

TD 

At the beginning of this year, Danske Bank said it intended to focus on serving corporate clients and related individuals in the Baltic states and to gradually leave the retail banking segment.

“The sale is part of the execution of our strategy of being a Nordic bank that supports the needs of business customers also when they do business outside the Nordic region,” said Lars Stensgaard Mørch, Head of Business Banking at Danske Bank Group.

Swebank Latvia CEO Maris Mancinskis indicated that Swedbank has the infrastructure, resources and professional solutions to provide high-class banking services to its new clients. "This decision confirms that the Baltics are Swedbank's home market and we have long-term business plans in this region," Mancinskis said.

In Zauere's words, both parties are determined to ensure a smooth transfer of services and all the necessary support for clients whose contracts are being transferred.

After the banking regulators' permission is received, the transfer of banking services will be completed in the first quarter of 2016. The acquisition affects around 120,000 Danske Bank's customers in Lithuania with approximately 525 million euros of loans and 7,000 customers in Latvia with approximately 116 million euros of loans.

"As soon as the official permissions from the banking regulators are received, clients will be sent detailed information about the transition process and how it will affect the services they are using. For the time being, the clients do not have to take any action. Until further notice, all services will be provided as usual," the Danske Bank spokeswoman said.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank reported a 464,000 euros profit for the first half of 2015, which was 2.3 times less than a year ago.

Danske Bank operates in Scandinavia and the Baltic states, as well as the UK and Ireland.

Riga newsroom, +371 6708 8606, eko_zinas@bns.lv

HD Danske Bank signs agreement to sell their Lithuanian and Latvian personal banking business to Swedbank
WC 363 words
PD 23 September 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, September 23 (ELTA) - Danske Bank has concluded an agreement with Swedbank Lithuania and Swedbank Latvia on selling its retail business. The transaction covers personal accounts, loans, deposits, payment cards and securities. At this stage documents will be submitted to the Competition Council seeking approval to the transaction, as well as respective institutions in Latvia, Danske Bank said in a statement.

Earlier this year Danske Bank announced its intention to focus activities in the three Baltic countries on corporate and private banking, while gradually exiting from the mass market personal banking business.

TD 

"The sale is part of the execution of our strategy of being a Nordic bank that supports the needs of business customers also when they do business outside the Nordic region," says Lars Stensgaard Morch, Head of Business Banking at Danske Bank Group. "We want to develop our business banking operations for local as well as Nordic customers by enhancing the product offering, drawing on Danske Bank's broad product range and innovative solutions".

"Having long-term customer service experience, we can offer both convenient finance management tools and professional advisory. We constantly develop our customer service, electronic solutions and broaden the scope of financial services in order to reflect modern banking trends and changing customer needs," says Dovile Grigiene, Head of Swedbank Lithuania.

Both parties have committed to ensure smooth transfer of services and all needed assistance to the customers who are subject to this transfer.

After receiving the approval it is expected to transfer services in the first quarter of 2016. Service transfer will affect around 120,000 private Danske Bank customers in Lithuania and 7,000 customers in Latvia. The size of the loan portfolio, subject to this transfer, is approximately EUR 525 million in Lithuania and EUR 116 million in Latvia.

Once formal approval from Competition Council is granted, customers will be contacted directly with full details of the transfer process and how this will affect their accounts with Danske. In the meantime, customers need take no action and all products and services will continue as normal until further notice.

Karolis Broga

HD Swedbank may become Lithuania’s largest bank through deal with Danske Bank
WC 282 words
PD 23 September 2015
ET 09:34
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Sept 23, BNS - Swedbank, one of Lithuania’s largest commercial banks, may become the country’s largest bank by assets after the acquisition of Danske Bank’s Lithuanian retail banking business, which will increase the number of Swedbank’s retail customers to more than 1.4 million and its loan portfolio to approximately 2.5 billion euros.

“It [the deal with Danske Bank] is the usual business practice,” Dovile Grigiene, the head of Swedbank Lithuania, told BNS.

TD 

As of late June, Swedbank had 1.328 million private customers with a loan portfolio of 1.97 billion euros. It will take over approximately 120,000 private customers and a loan portfolio of about 525 million euros from Danske Bank.

Moreover, Swedbank will also take over personal accounts, deposits, payment cards and securities of private customers of the Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank. Details about these assets have not yet been disclosed.

Loans are part of a bank’s assets hence Swedbank may become Lithuania’s largest bank by assets after the closure of the deal. At the end of June, Swedbank group ranked second in Lithuania with assets worth 6.216 billion euros, after SEB Bankas with 6.468 billion euros.

Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, said on Wednesday that it had signed an agreement with the Lithuanian and Latvian units of the Scandinavian financial group Swedbank on the sale of its retail banking business in the two countries.

The deal is expected to be closed in the first quarter of 2016.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8520

HD Press Release: Odfjell SE : Refinancing
WC 261 words
PD 25 September 2015
ET 09:02
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

Odfjell SE has entered into a term loan facility agreement with DNB Bank 
ASA, Danske Bank AS, DVB Bank America N.V and Swedbank AB for 
refinancing of existing loans on the vessels Bow Sea, Bow Sun and Bow 
Summer. DNB Bank ASA is acting as the agent bank and the total loan is 
USD 112 million. The loan has a 5-year term with 10-year profile. 
 
   Odfjell Asia II Pte Ltd, indirectly fully owned by Odfjell SE, has 
entered into a term loan facility agreement with Nordea Bank Norge for 
refinancing of existing loans on the vessels Bow Dalian, Bow Fuling, Bow 
Nangang and Bow Star. The total loan is USD 78.5 million. The loan has a 
5-year term with 13-year profile. 
 
   This means that we have completed all scheduled vessel refinancing in 
2015. The refinancing will give Odfjell SE USD 43.8 million in added 
liquidity. 
 
   For further information:

HD Danish regulator warns Danske Bank on Swedish growth strategy
WC 313 words
PD 9 October 2015
ET 08:58
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Oct 9 (Reuters) - Denmark's Financial Services Authority (FSA) has warned the country's largest bank, Danske Bank, that there is a substantial risk in its growth strategy in neighbouring Sweden, where real estate prices continue to rise rapidly.

Danske Bank has seen significant growth in lending to Swedish property companies this year and last year, and also plans increased lending to buyers of private homes in the country, the FSA noted in a statement on Friday.

TD 

"Given the current situation in the Swedish property market the bank is taking a substantial risk of significant future losses with the chosen growth strategy," the FSA said.

The FSA said the bank should ensure a thorough credit evaluation of its Swedish customers and carefully consider whether the property market's development "provides a basis to change the strategy".

In Sweden it is normal practice to grant 50-year floating-rate, interest-only mortgages for up to 70-75 per cent of a the market value of a home, and in some cases Danske Bank had granted deferred amortization for up to 80 percent of the value, the FSA said.

Swedish real estate prices were up 15.3 percent in August from a year earlier, figures from the Nasdaq OMX Valueguard-KTH Housing Index (HOX) showed last month.

A boom in Swedish home prices since the late 1990s has driven up household debt to some of the highest levels in Europe.

Danske Bank's growth has been lagging its Nordic peers since the financial crisis in 2008 due to a bursting of property bubbles in both Denmark and Ireland, two of its main markets at the time.

Danske Bank was not immediately available for a comment. (Reporting by Teis Jensen, additional reporting by Ole Mikkelsen, editing by Terje Solsvik)

HD Exec: Danske Bank will seek to become Lithuania’s leader in business banking – daily
WC 139 words
PD 13 October 2015
ET 02:04
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Oct 13, BNS - Danske Bank, which has sold its Lithuanian retail banking business to Swedbank, will seek to become Lithuania’s leader in business banking, an executive of the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets has said.

“We seek to become Lithuania’s leaders in business banking. This includes both small and medium-sized enterprises as well as larger companies and international corporations. It makes no difference to us,” Mikael Ericsson told the Verslo Zinios business daily.

TD 

The group had not set a target for its business loan portfolio growth yet expected that its planned 15-million-euro investment in IT infrastructure would help achieve this leadership goal, he added.

HD Press Release: Tikkurila's commercial paper program renewed
WC 298 words
PD 14 October 2015
ET 08:00
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

Tikkurila Oyj 
 
   Stock Exchange Release 
 
   October 14, 2015 at 3:00 p.m. (CET+1) 
 
   Tikkurila Oyj renews its commercial paper program, effective from 
October 14, 2015, so that the maximum aggregate nominal value of the 
program will be EUR 150 million. This will replace the current EUR 100 
million commercial paper program. Based on this new program, Tikkurila 
Oyj can issue unsecured debt with a maturity of less than one year into 
the Finnish money markets via Danske Bank Oyj and Pohjola Pankki Oyj. 
This change does not cause any arrangement costs. The revolving credit 
facility of the bank financing agreement, announced in June 2015, acts 
as a back-up facility for the revised commercial paper program. 
 
   This revision aims to increase the flexibility of Group's short-term 
debt financing, to enable replacing some other forms of financing with 
direct debt from the markets, and to extend the base of potential 
investors. 
 
   Tikkurila OyjJukka Havia, CFO

region and Russia. With our roots in Finland, we now operate in 16 
countries. Our high-quality products and extensive services ensure the 
best possible user experience in the market. Sustainable beauty since 
1862.
